        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413547121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2652447700747558330">I really love this story, because in it we see Anita going after a lycanthrope with a court order of execution for the first time. The fact that Zerbrowski is in it certainly doesn't hurt, either. ;-)<br/><br/>There are actually two storylines in this book: one involves the aforementioned lycanthrope, who <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[is a serial killer killing women in especially gruesome ways. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The other, unconnected, is about Musette, Belle Morte's representative, and the vampires she brought with her </span>
  <span id="freeText2652447700747558330" style="display:none">I really love this story, because in it we see Anita going after a lycanthrope with a court order of execution for the first time. The fact that Zerbrowski is in it certainly doesn't hurt, either. ;-)<br /><br />There are actually two storylines in this book: one involves the aforementioned lycanthrope, who <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[is a serial killer killing women in especially gruesome ways. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The other, unconnected, is about Musette, Belle Morte's representative, and the vampires she brought with her to visit Jean-Claude, et.al.<br /><br />This is the first book in which Anita is a Federal Marshal. And Jean-Claude <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[becomes his own <i>sourdre de sang</i>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Richard decides <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[to live, but along the way he's a cruel bastard. I really don't like him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Also, this is the book in which <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Dolph completely loses it and is put on enforced leave <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. All of these things together combine into an amazing story for me, so I always feel that it's a five star read despite the below issues.<br /><br />Interestingly, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9317896.Narcissus_in_Chains__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___10_" title="Narcissus in Chains (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #10) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Narcissus in Chains</a> Anita learned that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Micah had been lying to her by omission in pretty major ways, but though rocked by the news, she never hesitated around him in any way. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25925179.Cerulean_Sins__Anita_Blake__Vampire_Hunter___11_" title="Cerulean Sins (Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter, #11) by Laurell K. Hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Cerulean Sins</a>, she still doesn't exhibit any signs of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[holding a grudge. We the readers weren't ever told why this was, and Anita should have held a grudge. Not holding one doesn't fit her character. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I find it odd that the <u>NiC</u> revelation was revealed and forgotten.<br /><br />I have some problems with <u>Cerulean Sins</u>, but they're continuity errors and I love the story enough to forgive them. The biggest continuity error is in the time of events in this story. On page 1, line 1: "It was early September, a busy time of year for raising the dead." In Chapter 2, page 18: "... his deep voice came clear in the still October night." In Chapter 4, page 35: "She was due three months from now, just after Thanksgiving. So what the hell was she doing in town a month and some change before Halloween?" <br /><br />So is the story happening in September, October, or August? And that last quote is a contradiction in and of itself: How can it be three months until "just after Thanksgiving" but it's only "a month and some change before Halloween"? If you ignore the Thanksgiving reference, this quote puts the time of events back in "early September." <br /><br />In the final chapter, Chapter 62, the time is again confirmed as September: Page 529, "Summer is over and gone, but autumn is here, and next month is October with the bluest skies of the year."<br /><br />I don't understand how LKH could confuse her timeline like this, but I blame the editor for not catching this continuity issue and fixing it before it made it into print.<br /><br />Another continuity issue was that Jamil is now Hati. We have two quotes that say this: on page 270, in Chapter 30, "Jamil being a good Hati..." and in Chapter 47, on page 427, "Jamil and Shang-Da, his Hati and Skoll..." In previous books, Jamil was Sköll and Shang-Da was Hati. Again, I blame the editor for not catching this mistake, though I wonder how LKH could have made it in the first place.<br /><br />And lastly, on page 59 we are told that Damian is only 600 years old. In previous books he was 1,000. Again, I don't understand how LKH made this mistake but I blame the editor for not catching it.<br /><br />Because I blame the editor for not correcting the aforementioned issues, I don't let these errors negatively impact my rating for this story. Besides, the story was long and these lines were few and far between, so they were soon forgotten.<br /><br />My pet peeve reared its ugly head in this book, too: "writhe" was used eight times in its various tenses. In one scene, it was used four times! In close succession! (This was on pages 210-211. Three of the instances were on page 211.)<br /><br />And finally, in both <u>Narcissus in Chains</u> and <u>Cerulean Sins</u>, the wolf pack clan name has been spelled differently from how it was first introduced, but at least it's been consistent in these two books: "Thronnos Rokke."<br /><br />Things I liked were included in the first three paragraphs of this review. There were also many lines that made me smile in this text, but I only noted down one of them. I think this is the one I liked the best (the <u>underlined</u> part is for those lines that made me smile, the rest is for context):<br /><br />1. From Chapter 8, closer to the beginning than the middle (my edition: page 72):<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <blockquote>I opened my mouth to call her a heartless bitch, but it wasn't what came out. "Did you believe that gifts worthy of such beauty could be hurried? Would you really take some poor substitute in the place of the magnificence we had commissioned?"<br /><u>I stopped talking. All of our men were staring at me, except Damian, who was hugging me for all he was worth.<br />"Ventriloquism," Jason said, from the other side of Jean-Claude, "it's the only answer."<br />Jean-Claude nodded. "A miracle, indeed."</u> ...</blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><i>Most recent (penultimate?) reread of <u>Cerulean Sins</u> was from February 19 to 20, 2014.<br /><b>This current reread took place from July 17 to 18, 2015. :-)</b></i><br /><br /><b>The following spoiler is a chapter-by-chapter synopsis of what happens in the book. I wrote it for myself and I'm going to try to keep spoilers out of it, but I'm going to hide it just in case...</b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Chapter 1: Anita meets with a potential client.<br /><br />Chapter 2: Anita talks with some of the witnesses at Lindel Cemetery, where she has a zombie to raise.<br /><br />Chapter 3: Anita raises a zombie in front of lawyers, the widow, cops and a judge; Asher arrives when all is done.<br /><br />Chapter 4: Musette has arrived early in town. Anita doesn't understand why they can't punish her for it.<br /><br />Chapter 5: Anita talks with Asher, Damian and Jason in the parking lot of Circus of the Damned.<br /><br />Chapter 6: Jean-Claude meets Anita and crew when they get downstairs.<br /><br />Chapter 7: Musette has gifts for Jean-Claude and Asher.<br /><br />Chapter 8: Anita is outmaneuvered; Musette claims Asher as her guest gift.<br /><br />Chapter 9: Anita does not let Musette's insult go unanswered.<br /><br />Chapter 10: Anita talks with Jean-Claude. They discuss their people and how to make them safe.<br /><br />Chapter 11: Asher is reluctant. Anita doesn't want him to go.<br /><br />Chapter 12: Asher disrobes, with help.<br /><br />Chapter 13: Jean-Claude and Asher die at dawn.<br /><br />Chapter 14: Asher didn't hold back; Anita succumbs to the effects.<br /><br />Chapter 15: Jason helps Anita; Dolph and Zerbrowski call, need her at a crime scene.<br /><br />Chapter 16: At crime scene #1, the cop on duty doesn't want to let Anita through. But she is a federal marshal now, so he can't keep her out.<br /><br />Chapter 17: Zerbrowski sees how sick Anita is and tries to get her to go home.<br /><br />Chapter 18: Anita looks over crime scene #1, confirms Detective Reynolds' suppositions.<br /><br />Chapter 19: Detective Merlioni is the first person Anita sees at crime scene #2.<br /><br />Chapter 20: Dolph is unprofessional at the second crime scene; Anita is sick.<br /><br />Chapter 21: Anita comes to in the bathroom with Detective Reynolds. Jason takes her out and home.<br /><br />Chapter 22: Anita comes to in the bathtub with Micah. She discovers why she's been so sick; they talk about that and Richard.<br /><br />Chapter 23: Anita's in bed; Micah has to leave, so Nathaniel is brought in to sleep with Anita.<br /><br />Chapter 24: Jason takes one for the team; he and Anita talk about her relationships.<br /><br />Chapter 25: Anita takes a shower; Jamil arrives with a very sick Richard.<br /><br />Chapter 26: Nathaniel helps Anita; they're moving temporarily to the Circus. Zerbrowski is on the phone.<br /><br />Chapter 27: Caleb took a message from Zerbrowski; he also was told to stay close to Anita today.<br /><br />Chapter 28: Belle Morte pays Anita another visit.<br /><br />Chapter 29: "The Mother of all Darkness" is curious.<br /><br />Chapter 30: Anita and crew are being followed again. She was going to call Bobby Lee for advice, when Richard's hunger overwhelmed her.<br /><br />Chapter 31: Anita feeds the <i>ardeur</i> with Jean-Claude, then they talk about blood-letting. Asher joins them in the bathroom and the mood is lost.<br /><br />Chapter 32: Anita talks with Jean-Claude and Asher: "I don't even get an hour to digest that you used vampire wiles on me."<br /><br />Chapter 33: Nathaniel finds Anita in the hallway outside the bedroom and tells her that the guys who followed them are back.<br /><br />Chapter 34: Anita strategizes with Bobby Lee; Claudia proves that men see her as just a girl, despite the fact that she is "six-freaking-feet and six-fucking-inches tall."<br /><br />Chapter 35: Anita and crew corner the bad guys who were following her; the police arrive.<br /><br />Chapter 36: Anita talks with an unfriendly detective; a clueless detective walks up and spills the beans about the prisoners.<br /><br />Chapter 37: Anita recognizes two of Heinrick's associates, but the photos aren't of high enough quality for her to place them. The detective in charge won't let her make copies of the photos.<br /><br />Chapter 38: Jean-Claude calls: the police have taken Jason.<br /><br />Chapter 39: Dolph shoots himself in the foot, metaphorically speaking.<br /><br />Chapter 40: Anita talks with Jason on the way back to the Circus; she offends him, too.<br /><br />Chapter 41: Anita talks with Bobby Lee about Heinrick, mercenaries.<br /><br />Chapter 42: Jean-Claude and Asher are dressed in their banquet finery. They talk with Anita, apologize.<br /><br />Chapter 43: Anita talks with Jean-Claude, Asher and Micah. They tell her of a plot they plan to enact.<br /><br />Chapter 44: Anita wonders why there are plates on the floor in the banquet room. Jean-Claude, then Asher join her. Valentina shares her memory of the Dark.<br /><br />Chapter 45: Musette's side breaks truce first. Anita evens the playing field so that the guards can take Musette to her room, when Belle Morte manifests.<br /><br />Chapter 46: Belle Morte tries to control Anita, the leopards, Jean-Claude's vampires.<br /><br />Chapter 47: Richard found his backbone and he's being a cruel bastard at the worst of times.<br /><br />Chapter 48: Belle Morte doesn't follow Richard's directions. Jean-Claude becomes <i>sourdre de sang</i> of his own line.<br /><br />Chapter 49: Belle Morte can save Asher. Richard steps up.<br /><br />Chapter 50: Anita finds that she can give Asher the power he needs to restore himself. Richard, naturally, doesn't understand.<br /><br />Chapter 51: Asher is restored; Belle Morte and company leave, but Valentina and Bartolomé stay.<br /><br />Chapter 52: Zerbrowski calls: he has a fresh murder scene for Anita to come look at.<br /><br />Chapter 53: At the new murder scene, Anita stalls before investigating the bathtub's contents.<br /><br />Chapter 54: Anita searches the tub.<br /><br />Chapter 55: Special Agent Bradford shares a clue. Zerbrowski mobilizes.<br /><br />Chapter 56: Detective O'Brien tries to play top dog.<br /><br />Chapter 57: Heinrick answers some questions. Something went very wrong when Mobile Reserve tried to apprehend Van Anders.<br /><br />Chapter 58: Van Anders escaped; Anita learns that she knows more than the feds.<br /><br />Chapter 59: Anita gets Richard to agree to let her use werewolves to track Van Anders.<br /><br />Chapter 60: The wolves lead Anita to Van Anders. He is taken by surprise.<br /><br />Chapter 61: Anita takes comfort from Micah, talks on the phone with Agent Bradford.<br /><br />Chapter 62: Denouement. <blockquote>... I'm learning that you have to make time for what's important. You have to fight to carve little pieces of happiness out of your life, or the everyday emergencies will eat up everything.<br />When we finish <i>Charlotte's Web</i> Nathaniel want to read <i>Treasure Island</i>. Sounds good to me. <i>[fin]</i></blockquote><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14586169034303854654">I was honestly so utterly bored while reading this. I'm so sad at how this series has become, I used to love it so much.<br/><br/>What baffled me the most was how such a long book has barely anything going on in it.<br/><br/>The only redeeming quality was Jason, I love him so much, I felt like he was voicing my every thought LOL</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1528196102">

<div id="review_896173893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/896173893" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29879130-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395506412p2/29879130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/896173893?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/29879130-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer896173893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15655687923466911077">I'm finally waving my white flag. I can't bear to read this garbage any more. Back in '99-'00 I read the Anita Blake series up to that point (Blue Moon?) and enjoyed it. It opened up a new love of Urban Fantasy (which is still my favorite genre) so I continued to read the books as they came out over the years until "Kiss the Dead". I couldn't make it through that pile of shit. Recently I thought maybe I had been right in thinking the beginning books were good....surely I couldn't have been compl</span>
  <span id="freeText15655687923466911077" style="display:none">I'm finally waving my white flag. I can't bear to read this garbage any more. Back in '99-'00 I read the Anita Blake series up to that point (Blue Moon?) and enjoyed it. It opened up a new love of Urban Fantasy (which is still my favorite genre) so I continued to read the books as they came out over the years until "Kiss the Dead". I couldn't make it through that pile of shit. Recently I thought maybe I had been right in thinking the beginning books were good....surely I couldn't have been completely wrong? I have read many, many books between then and now so I needed to know if my memory of the beginning of the series was correct. I was half-right. The beginning of the series is exponentially better than #10-#21. Reading through these books has made me realize what an absolutely awful writer LKH is. She needs to stop. No, we need to stop paying her to play out her creepy fantasies on paper. <br /><br />Anita. I can hardly put into words how truly terrible she is as a character. Although, you can hardly blame the character herself. She didn't even have a chance. She is the embodiment of LKH in this world where she is perfect, the most admired, the sexiest, the smartest (choking on effing laughter), the bravest, the only one with all the answers and most importantly, the most superior. In truth, Anita is dumb as a rock. She is engaging in constant pissing contests, bullying her way into business that isn't hers, seeks reasons to kill/murder, looks down on every single person who grabs her attention and is so completely immature you couldn't possibly have any respect for her. It's impossible to sympathize with her, like her or root for her. It's horrible how transparent LKH is in this series. I'm sure I can't be the only person who feels like they know way too much about LKH.....insecure, lonely, poor fashion sense, sexually repressed and because it's so obvious I need to say it again, insecure. <br /><br />Women, other than Anita, are either pathetic or batshit crazy. Police are completely unprofessional. The one person who might have been respected by Anita in this series, Dolph, loses his goddamn, bigoted mind in this book, completing the image in Anita's head that she is superior to all. All of Anita's "men" are short, long haired, pretty and most importantly, submissive to her. It's goddamn creepy to be reading someone else's fantasy.....that needs to stay in your head LKH. She has the potential to be creative and write exciting, action-filled books (if not very "deep"). Instead she uses her imagination to create a world where she can live and have the sex life she wants through a self-absorbed, pitiful excuse for a heroine. <br /><br />I'm actually pissed at myself and insulted by LKH. First, yes, I'm angry with myself for buying these books. I knew by book 9 they were starting to go downhill and that by "Kiss the Dead" they would be unreadable but I bought a few more. I have only myself to blame but it stops now. I won't buy any more, I won't support LKH's Anitaverse so she can take her weird vacation from reality. I'm insulted by LKH because she feels like she can keep churning out this trash like she ever deserved to be on the Best Sellers list. I've read far superior writers who never made it on the list but somehow we've all encouraged poor writing and non-existent editing by buying this waste of paper. We need better standards people!! Do you know how much money these books have made?!?! Over 6 million dollars. For this shit. We have paid over 6 million dollars for the worst that writing has to offer. I'm ashamed. I'm off to cleanse my conscience with a better book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15655687923466911077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156203574" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156203574" />
    <a title="Barb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5085328-barb"><img alt="Barb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424825656p2/5085328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156203574?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barb" href="/user/show/5085328-barb">Barb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780425188361" href="/book/show/705743.Cerulean_Sins">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156203574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17709774349223100215">Cerulean Sins is the eleventh book in the Anita Blake Vampire Hunter Series. In this episode, Ms. Blake is contacted by a man she quickly pegs as a hired assassin who says he wants to hire her for the purpose of raising one of his ancestors from the dead. As you follow the story, you discover that Ms. Blake is more than a “vampire hunter”. She is an animator, macromancer, part shapeshifter, and the girl friend of the Master Vampire. After completing a successful session of “animating” (raising a</span>
  <span id="freeText17709774349223100215" style="display:none">Cerulean Sins is the eleventh book in the Anita Blake Vampire Hunter Series. In this episode, Ms. Blake is contacted by a man she quickly pegs as a hired assassin who says he wants to hire her for the purpose of raising one of his ancestors from the dead. As you follow the story, you discover that Ms. Blake is more than a “vampire hunter”. She is an animator, macromancer, part shapeshifter, and the girl friend of the Master Vampire. After completing a successful session of “animating” (raising a dead man) to settle an insurance claim between the insurance company and the man’s widow, Ms. Blake becomes involved in trying to find a serial killer. All this at the same time she has major problems going on in her love life and major problems with the international politics of vampires, werewolves, and various “other worldly” creatures. <br /><br />This is the first of the Anita Blake series I have read. I admit I was quite excited about reading the book as I had heard some good things about some of her earlier books. However, I was extremely disappointed as I began to read the book. Most of the first half of the book was really one long, group sex act. Unfortunately, the sex had little to do with the plot and serves only to fill a good number of pages. The second half of the book did have a little more of a plot with some bit of mystery and some detective work. For me, it was too little to late. If I had not been reviewing the book I would have stopped reading after the first 50 or so pages and tossed it in the trash. <br /><br />Ms. Hamilton’s writing is quite good and I believe she could have produced an excellent book with the serial killer plot, if she would have gotten down to business and developed the plot, instead of turning out page after dreary page of vampire sex. However, taken as it was written, the characters are ok but the author really didn’t make me care about any of them. Some of the characters had so many problems I should have felt some sympathy for them and should have continued to read with an expectant hope that their problems would come to a positive conclusion. That, however, was not the case. When I finished the book I mentally said, “That’s nice,” but I truly had no vested emotions in any of the characters. Further, I was really disappointed that in something called a “vampire hunter series” the hunter didn’t “hunt” any vampires; instead, she had group sex with them. What is that about? <br /><br />I really wanted to like this book. I like stories about vampires and other scary stuff. What I didn’t want was a pornographic tale that ran for some 200+ pages of a 400-page book. It is a shame because I believe Ms. Hamilton could have produced a really great book. To say I was let down is an understatement. I am sorry to say that it will likely be a very long time before I read another Laurell Hamilton book. <br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17709774349223100215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36972219" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36972219" />
    <a title="Mari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1687185-mari"><img alt="Mari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523823472p2/1687185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36972219?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari" href="/user/show/1687185-mari">Mari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mari by: </span>
      Mike
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1687185-mari?shelf=supernatural-romance">supernatural-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36972219" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7609323527108220844">Now that I've read all the other books in the series, lovely Mike bought me the latest, "Cerulean Sins" as a Christmas present. I wanted to wait to finish other books before I started this one - but of course I have no will power, and I read it immediately. <br/><br/>If, dear readers, you've read the books leading up to this one, you know that our heroine, Anita Blake, has gone from being celibate to boinking nearly everyone in the books. This story is no exception. I won't divulge who - but I doubt you'd</span>
  <span id="freeText7609323527108220844" style="display:none">Now that I've read all the other books in the series, lovely Mike bought me the latest, "Cerulean Sins" as a Christmas present. I wanted to wait to finish other books before I started this one - but of course I have no will power, and I read it immediately. <br /><br />If, dear readers, you've read the books leading up to this one, you know that our heroine, Anita Blake, has gone from being celibate to boinking nearly everyone in the books. This story is no exception. I won't divulge who - but I doubt you'd be surprised. Aside from the drastic morality shift, the only two annoyances to the plot are the main character's continuing badly timed guilt, and the increasing predictability of the crimes she investigates. The bad guys get increasingly bad - but she has increasing power to deal with them. Here's the basic equation:<br /><br />Step One: Bad guys arrive in town and challenge one or all of the triumvirate (Richard/Jean-Claude/Anita). (Usually there is also some really horrendous crime committed - but not always related to the Bad (Supernatural) Guy.)<br /><br />Step Two: An action, usually unethical/immoral/repugnant is the key to increasing power and thus defeating Bad Guy.<br /><br />Step Three: Agonize over the decision.<br /><br />Step Four: Do it anyway.<br /><br />Step Five: Feel guilty.<br /><br />Step Six: Beat the Bad Guy, but not before being introduced (somewhere in the plot) to a new imminent Badder Guy, that will probably arrive in the next novel.<br /><br />Step Seven: Feel a bit more guilty. Think about Richard. Sum up.<br /><br />I can't complain too much because having a successful formula will keep your fans happy and you employed. I just miss the mysteries being a bit more complicated. Though portions of the book are quite good - the main plot was just to obvious. The character, Anita Blake, seems to have only one weakness now - her own battle with her morality - which seems to get a bit more trite in every succeeding book. The secondary characters hold much of the interest now - particularly Asher, the old lover of Jean Claude. In fact, in several instances it is those characters that propel the story forward - especially Jason in this instance. Jason finally calls Anita on her feelings of guilt and angst - and draws attention to her defense mechanisms that are making her life harder and more complicated than it needs to be. I wouldn't have thought of his character as being the analytical type - but if follows the plot well.<br /><br />That's it for now. Not exactly a thumbs up - but not a thumbs down either. I still buy the next book, of course, because I'm addicted and hopeful that I'll be surprised. We'll see. . .<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7609323527108220844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10118474085239091398">Reading the series nonstop has been both a blessing and a curse.<br/>I loved Anita from the start for her stubborn, bitchy attitude that never ceases to amaze me.<br/>The plot is well written, the series constant and the consequences of each of the character's actions and decisions rational and complicates the story.<br/>And the men, :)<br/>Oh, Laurell, the men.   <span id="freeText10118474085239091398" style="display:none">Reading the series nonstop has been both a blessing and a curse.<br />I loved Anita from the start for her stubborn, bitchy attitude that never ceases to amaze me.<br />The plot is well written, the series constant and the consequences of each of the character's actions and decisions rational and complicates the story.<br />And the men, :)<br />Oh, Laurell, the men. XD<br />Jean-Clause has been a constant, always beside Anita, always the seductive vampire.<br />Richard is an ASSHOLE.<br />Micah is a new addition and I can't wait to arrive to Book Thirteen because Micah so far has been the most agreeable of the men in Anita's life. He has been helpful and Anita belonged to him as her Nimir-Raj, which makes things screwed up.<br />Nathaniel is...is...I'm speechless. I can't even imagine how different Nathaniel's position in Anita's life is compared to the other contenders. He awakens Anita's protective instinct and at the same time attracts her. At first he strives for Anita to own him but gradually I feel like Nathaniel is going to want more as her pomme de sang.<br />Asher is a story I don't know how Anita will end. He is broken, emotionally damaged and constantly insecure of his scars. Anita shows a softer side when it comes to Asher because she accepts Asher and finds him beautiful still. I loved that about Anita.<br />&lt;3<br />I love this series. And I can't wait for what will Anita do next.</span>

<div id="review_1191904425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191904425" />
    <a title="Anna &#39;Bookbuyer&#39;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5783783-anna-bookbuyer"><img alt="Anna &#39;Bookbuyer&#39;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589481290p2/5783783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

  <span id="freeText9820112632711582353" style="display:none">I'm really starting to hate the old vampires. Why can't just one be normal. -.-<br /><br />Thank god Jean Claude is now his own soudre de sangue and therefore can protect Asher. It was almost too late but thankfully Anita has her own powers that helped Asher.<br /><br />Thankfully Belle was put in her place. I really dislike her. <br /><br />The idea of vampire children really disturbs me. I'm glad that it is considered taboo and that Belle killed the pedophile vampire that created Valentina.<br /><br />The idea that people wanted Anita for her ability to raise the dead is a bit strange to me but when it was explained it made sense. I'm glad that her mentor's coven were worried about her karma and therefore made it so the bad guys didn't want her. lol.<br /><br />Edit: August 2020<br /><br />I lol'ed at my top comment. The old vampires are weird. :P<br /><br />I still have mixed feelings about Asher because of later in the books but I'm glad he's alive...<br /><br />Belle being told that Anita would kill her was hilarious. Belle truly acted like she was some immortal god and a human told her it was going to kill her. 🤦‍♀️ Not as bad as Obsidian Butterfly but similar.<br /><br />I hate all the references to pedophilia in this series. Nathaniel, Gregory, Stephan, Valentina, and kind of Bartolome. <br /><br />I'm glad the shapshifter serial killer is dead. The way he was so sure Anita couldn't kill him made me smile.</span>

Anita has been reduced from a kick as heroine to a whiny inflatable sex doll. Insert penis here. We don't even need a relationship build up cuz it can all be explained by the ardeur. Eye roll. I love a good adult book but I want to read actual charac</span>
  <span id="freeText1898001950887916594" style="display:none">I'm calling it. This series is officially dead to me. Hamilton isn't even pretending there's a plot anymore. Anita has been reduced from a kick as heroine to a whiny inflatable sex doll. Insert penis here. We don't even need a relationship build up cuz it can all be explained by the ardeur. Eye roll.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mE1agCwUV5nYButWKweZLXaWdJVC2AFIMKH7eb+nxjgL3dQKzlt/lqnGD+s2wrXUuMN8mi/PZUzGwcnpcadaiw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7siB5xbzz+3YamwCv8SmGPl9TkLIyavRJLXfULjnhI99WA9t9Lzn4qmqiL+iAYrhNyhGTaXez9XS1e3AducYPA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2164227006548831104">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series.   <span id="freeText2164227006548831104" style="display:none">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis with her family.</span>
